<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Middle East</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Geopolitical region encompassing Egypt and most of Western Asia, including Iran</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">MENA</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Greater_Middle_East" title="Greater Middle East">Greater Middle East</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Middle_East_(disambiguation)" title="Middle East (disambiguation)">Middle East (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Middle_east.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="938" data-file-width="1005" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Middle_east.jpg/260px-Middle_east.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Middle_east.jpg/390px-Middle_east.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Middle_east.jpg/520px-Middle_east.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Middle_east.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Middle East between Africa, Europe, Central Asia, and Southern Asia.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/260px-Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/390px-Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/520px-Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Middle East map of Köppen climate classification.</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Middle East</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar">الشرق الأوسط</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/ISO_233" title="ISO 233">ISO 233</a>:</small> <span title="Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="ar-Latn">ash-Sharq al-Awsat</i></span>) is a geopolitical region commonly encompassing <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabia</a> (including the Arabian Peninsula and <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>), <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Asia Minor</a> (Asian part of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> except <a href="/wiki/Hatay_Province" title="Hatay Province">Hatay Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">East Thrace</a> (European part of Turkey), <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Syria_(region)" title="Syria (region)">Ash-Shām</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Socotra_Governorate" title="Socotra Governorate">Socotra Archipelago</a> (a part of <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>). The term came into widespread usage as a replacement of the term <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a> (as opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>) beginning in the early 20th century. The term "Middle East" has led to some confusion over its changing definitions, and has been viewed by some to be discriminatory<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dont_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-dont-2">[2]</a></sup> or too <a href="/wiki/Eurocentrism" title="Eurocentrism">Eurocentric</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hanafi_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-hanafi-3">[3]</a></sup> The region includes the vast majority of the territories included in the closely associated definition of <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>), but without the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a>, and additionally includes all of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> (not just the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai Region</a>) and all of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (not just the part barring <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">East Thrace</a>).
</p><p>Most Middle Eastern countries (13 out of 18) are part of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Middle_Eastern_countries_by_population" title="List of Middle Eastern countries by population">most populous countries in the region</a> are Egypt, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, and Turkey, while <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> is the largest Middle Eastern country by area. The <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Middle_East" title="History of the Middle East">history of the Middle East</a> dates back to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">ancient times</a>, with the geopolitical importance of the region being recognized for millennia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Several major religions have their origins in the Middle East, including <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> constitute the main socioethnic grouping in the region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persians" title="Persians">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azeris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copts" title="Copts">Copts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmen" title="Iraqi Turkmen">Iraqi Turkmen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">Yazidis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriots" title="Greek Cypriots">Greek Cypriots</a>.
</p><p>The Middle East generally has a hot, <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> climate, especially in the Peninsula and Egyptian regions. Several major rivers providing <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> to support <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> in limited areas here such as the <a href="/wiki/Nile_Delta" title="Nile Delta">Nile Delta</a> in Egypt, the <a href="/wiki/Tigris" title="Tigris">Tigris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euphrates" title="Euphrates">Euphrates</a> watersheds of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, and most of what is known as the <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a>. Conversely the Levantine coast and most of Turkey have more temperate, oceanic and wetter climates. Most of the countries that border the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> have vast reserves of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>, with monarchs of the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> in particular benefiting economically from petroleum exports. Because of the arid climate and heavy reliance on the fossil fuel industry, the Middle East is both <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa" title="Climate change in the Middle East and North Africa">a heavy contributor to climate change</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa" title="Climate change in the Middle East and North Africa">a region expected to be severely negatively impacted by it.</a>
</p><p>Other concepts of the region exist including the broader the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">Middle East and North Africa</a> (MENA), which includes states of the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, or the "<a href="/wiki/Greater_Middle_East" title="Greater Middle East">Greater Middle East</a>" which additionally also includes parts of <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span></h2>
<p>The term "Middle East" may have originated in the 1850s in the British <a href="/wiki/India_Office" title="India Office">India Office</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeaumontBlakeWagstaff198816_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeaumontBlakeWagstaff198816-9">[9]</a></sup> However, it became more widely known when <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> naval strategist <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Thayer_Mahan" title="Alfred Thayer Mahan">Alfred Thayer Mahan</a> used the term in 1902<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> to "designate the area between Arabia and India".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> During this time the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empires</a> were vying for influence in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, a rivalry which would become known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Game" title="Great Game">Great Game</a>. Mahan realized not only the strategic importance of the region, but also of its center, the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> He labeled the area surrounding the Persian Gulf as the Middle East, and said that after Egypt's <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>, it was the most important passage for Britain to control in order to keep the Russians from advancing towards <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Mahan first used the term in his article "The Persian Gulf and International Relations", published in September 1902 in the <i><a href="/wiki/National_Review_(London)" title="National Review (London)">National Review</a></i>, a British journal.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p> The Middle East, if I may adopt a term which I have not seen, will some day need <a href="/wiki/Malta_Protectorate" title="Malta Protectorate">its Malta</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">its Gibraltar</a>; it does not follow that either will be in the Persian Gulf.  Naval force has the quality of mobility which carries with it the privilege of temporary absences; but it needs to find on every scene of operation established bases of refit, of supply, and in case of disaster, of security. The British Navy should have the facility to concentrate in force if occasion arise, about <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aden_Province" title="Aden Province">Aden</a>, India, and the Persian Gulf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdelson199522–23_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdelson199522–23-16">[16]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Mahan's article was reprinted in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> and followed in October by a 20-article series entitled "The Middle Eastern Question," written by Sir <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ignatius_Valentine_Chirol" title="Ignatius Valentine Chirol">Ignatius Valentine Chirol</a>. During this series, Sir Ignatius expanded the definition of <i>Middle East</i> to include "those regions of Asia which extend to the borders of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> or command the approaches to India."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdelson199524_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdelson199524-17">[17]</a></sup> After the series ended in 1903, <i>The Times</i> removed quotation marks from subsequent uses of the term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdelson199526_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdelson199526-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Until <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, it was customary to refer to areas centered around <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and the eastern shore of the Mediterranean as the "<a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a>", while the "<a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>" centered on <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davison_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-davison-19">[19]</a></sup> and the Middle East then meant the area from <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a>, namely the area between the Near East and the Far East.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the late 1930s, the British established the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Command" title="Middle East Command">Middle East Command</a>, which was based in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, for its military forces in the region. After that time, the term "Middle East" gained broader usage in Europe and the United States, with the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Institute" title="Middle East Institute">Middle East Institute</a> founded in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> in 1946, among other usage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>The corresponding adjective is <i>Middle Eastern</i> and the derived noun is <i>Middle Easterner</i>.
</p><p>While non-Eurocentric terms such "Southwest Asia" or "Swasia" has been sparsedly used, the inclusion of an African country, Egypt, in the definition questions the usefulness of using such terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_and_criticism">Usage and criticism</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="805" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Middle_East.ogv" height="165" id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Middle_East.ogv/220px--Middle_East.ogv.jpg" preload="none" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="598769" data-framerate="29.97" data-height="300" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file, 400 × 300 (599 kbps)" data-width="400" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/44/Middle_East.ogv" type='video/ogg; codecs="theora, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="173728" data-framerate="29.97" data-height="120" data-shorttitle="VP9 120P" data-title="Lowest bandwidth VP9 (120P)" data-transcodekey="120p.vp9.webm" data-width="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/44/Middle_East.ogv/Middle_East.ogv.120p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="207184" data-framerate="29.97" data-height="160" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/44/Middle_East.ogv/Middle_East.ogv.160p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="242496" data-framerate="29.97" data-height="180" data-shorttitle="VP9 180P" data-title="Low bandwidth VP9 (180P)" data-transcodekey="180p.vp9.webm" data-width="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/44/Middle_East.ogv/Middle_East.ogv.180p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="321512" data-framerate="29.97" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/44/Middle_East.ogv/Middle_East.ogv.240p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="327896" data-framerate="29.97" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="VP9 240P" data-title="Small VP9 (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/44/Middle_East.ogv/Middle_East.ogv.240p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Middle_East.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1957 American film about the Middle East</div></div></div>
<p>The description <i>Middle</i> has also led to some confusion over changing definitions. Before the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>, "Near East" was used in English to refer to the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, while "Middle East" referred to the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">Persia</a>, and Arabian lands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In contrast, "<a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>" referred to the countries of <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>With the collapse of the Ottoman Empire in 1918, "Near East" largely fell out of common use in English, while "Middle East" came to be applied to the re-emerging countries of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_world" title="Islamic world">Islamic world</a>. However, the usage "Near East" was retained by a variety of academic disciplines, including <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">ancient history</a>, where it describes an area identical to the term <i>Middle East</i>, which is not used by these disciplines (see <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Near_East" title="Ancient Near East">Ancient Near East</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The first official use of the term "Middle East" by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">United States government</a> was in the 1957 <a href="/wiki/Eisenhower_Doctrine" title="Eisenhower Doctrine">Eisenhower Doctrine</a>, which pertained to the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a>. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Foster_Dulles" title="John Foster Dulles">John Foster Dulles</a> defined the Middle East as "the area lying between and including <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> on the west and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> on the east, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> on the North and the Arabian peninsula to the south, plus the <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davison_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-davison-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1958, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">State Department</a> explained that the terms "Near East" and "Middle East" were interchangeable, and defined the region as including only <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term <i>Middle East</i> has also been criticised by journalist Louay Khraish and historian <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Hanafi" title="Hassan Hanafi">Hassan Hanafi</a> for being a <a href="/wiki/Eurocentrism" title="Eurocentrism">Eurocentric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialist</a> term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dont_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-dont-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hanafi_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-hanafi-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> Stylebook says that Near East formerly referred to the farther west countries while Middle East referred to the eastern ones, but that now they are synonymous. It instructs:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Use <i>Middle East</i> unless <i>Near East</i> is used by a source in a story. <i>Mideast</i> is also acceptable, but <i>Middle East</i> is preferred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Translations">Translations</span></h3>
<p>There are terms similar to <i>Near East</i> and <i>Middle East</i> in other European languages, but since it is a relative description, the meanings depend on the country and are different from the English terms generally. In <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> the term <i><a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naher_Osten" title="de:Naher Osten">Naher Osten</a></i> (Near East) is still in common use (nowadays the term <i>Mittlerer Osten</i> is more and more common in press texts translated from English sources, albeit having a distinct meaning) and in <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%91%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA" title="ru:Ближний Восток">Ближний Восток</a> or <i>Blizhniy Vostok</i>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://bg.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%91%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B7%D1%8A%D0%BA_%D0%98%D0%B7%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA" title="bg:Близък Изток">Близкия Изток</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> <i><a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bliski_Wsch%C3%B3d" title="pl:Bliski Wschód">Bliski Wschód</a></i> or <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a> <i><a class="extiw" href="https://hr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bliski_istok" title="hr:Bliski istok">Bliski istok</a></i> (meaning <i>Near East</i> in all the four Slavic languages) remains as the only appropriate term for the region. However, some languages do have "Middle East" equivalents, such as the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moyen-Orient" title="fr:Moyen-Orient">Moyen-Orient</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://sv.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mellan%C3%B6stern" title="sv:Mellanöstern">Mellanöstern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oriente_Medio" title="es:Oriente Medio">Oriente Medio or Medio Oriente</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medio_Oriente" title="it:Medio Oriente">Medio Oriente</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[note 1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Perhaps because of the influence of the Western press, the Arabic equivalent of <i>Middle East</i> (Arabic: الشرق الأوسط  <i>ash-Sharq al-Awsaṭ</i>) has become standard usage in the mainstream Arabic press, comprising the same meaning as the term "Middle East" in North American and Western European usage. The designation, <i><a href="/wiki/Mashriq" title="Mashriq">Mashriq</a></i>, also from the Arabic root for <i>East</i>, also denotes a variously defined region around the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>, the eastern part of the Arabic-speaking world (as opposed to the <i><a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a></i>, the western part).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> Even though the term originated in the West, apart from Arabic, other languages of countries of the Middle East also use a translation of it. The <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> equivalent for Middle East is خاورمیانه (<i>Khāvar-e miyāneh</i>), the Hebrew is המזרח התיכון (<i>hamizrach hatikhon</i>), the Turkish is Orta Doğu and the Greek is Μέση Ανατολή (<i>Mesi Anatoli</i>).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_and_territory">Countries and territory</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Middle_Eastern_countries_by_population" title="List of Middle Eastern countries by population">List of Middle Eastern countries by population</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_and_territory_usually_considered_within_the_Middle_East">Countries and territory usually considered within the Middle East</span></h3>
<p>Traditionally included within the Middle East are <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Asia Minor</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">East Thrace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Socotra_Governorate" title="Socotra Governorate">Socotra Archipelago</a>. The region includes 17 UN-recognized countries and one <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a>. 
</p>

<dl><dd><small>a. <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1041539562">.mw-parser-output .citation{word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation:target{background-color:rgba(0,127,255,0.133)}</style><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_israel"><b><a href="#ref_israel">^</a></b></span> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_palestine"><b><a href="#ref_palestine">^</a></b></span> <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Law" title="Jerusalem Law">proclaimed capital of Israel</a>, which is <a href="/wiki/Status_of_Jerusalem" title="Status of Jerusalem">disputed</a>, and the actual location of the <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">Knesset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Israel" title="Supreme Court of Israel">Israeli Supreme Court</a>, and other governmental institutions of Israel. <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the actual location of the government of Palestine, whereas the proclaimed capital of Palestine is <a href="/wiki/East_Jerusalem" title="East Jerusalem">East Jerusalem</a>, which is <a href="/wiki/Status_of_Jerusalem" title="Status of Jerusalem">disputed</a>.</small></dd>
<dd><small>b. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_sanaa"><b><a href="#ref_sanaa">^</a></b></span> Controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Houthi_movement" title="Houthi movement">Houthis</a> due to the <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_Civil_War_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Yemeni Civil War (2014–present)">ongoing civil war</a>. Seat of government moved to Aden.</small></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_definitions_of_the_Middle_East">Other definitions of the Middle East</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Greater_Middle_East" title="Greater Middle East">Greater Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">MENA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a></div>
<p>Various concepts are often being paralleled to the Middle East, most notably the Near East, <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>. The Near East, Fertile Crescent, and Levant are geographical concepts, which refer to large sections of the modern-day Middle East, with the Near East being the closest to the Middle East in its geographical meaning. Due to it primarily being Arabic speaking, the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> region of North Africa is sometimes included.
</p><p>The countries of the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a>—<a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>—are occasionally included in definitions of the Middle East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Middle_East" title="Greater Middle East">Greater Middle East</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Political_geography" title="Political geography">political</a> term coined by the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">second Bush administration</a> in the first decade of the 21st century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haeri_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-haeri-34">[33]</a></sup> to denote various countries, pertaining to the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim world</a>, specifically <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> Various <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asian</a> countries are sometimes also included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Middle_East" title="History of the Middle East">History of the Middle East</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Neolithic#Western_Asia" title="Neolithic">Neolithic § Western_Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Near_East" title="Ancient Near East">Ancient Near East</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Middle_East" title="History of the Middle East">History of the Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uruk_period" title="Uruk period">Uruk period</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kish_civilization" title="Kish civilization">Kish civilization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_ancient_Levant" title="History of the ancient Levant">History of the ancient Levant</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Anatolia" title="History of Anatolia">History of Anatolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran" title="History of Iran">History of Iran</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern_Empires" title="Middle Eastern Empires">Middle Eastern Empires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pre-Islamic_Arabia" title="Pre-Islamic Arabia">Pre-Islamic Arabia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_modern_conflicts_in_the_Middle_East" title="List of modern conflicts in the Middle East">List of modern conflicts in the Middle East</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe,_Urfa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe%2C_Urfa.jpg/220px-G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe%2C_Urfa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe%2C_Urfa.jpg/330px-G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe%2C_Urfa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe%2C_Urfa.jpg/440px-G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe%2C_Urfa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe,_Urfa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Some <a href="/wiki/Henge" title="Henge">henges</a> at <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe" title="Göbekli Tepe">Göbekli Tepe</a> were erected as far back as <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe#Layer_III" title="Göbekli Tepe">9600 BC</a>, predating those of <a href="/wiki/Stonehenge" title="Stonehenge">Stonehenge</a>, England, by over seven millennia. The site of the oldest known man-made religious structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ArchMag_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-ArchMag-37">[36]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westernwall2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Westernwall2.jpg/220px-Westernwall2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Westernwall2.jpg/330px-Westernwall2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Westernwall2.jpg/440px-Westernwall2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westernwall2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Western_Wall" title="Western Wall">Western Wall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">Dome of the Rock</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jerusalem-Grabeskirche-14-vom_Erloeserkirchturm-2010-gje.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Jerusalem-Grabeskirche-14-vom_Erloeserkirchturm-2010-gje.jpg/220px-Jerusalem-Grabeskirche-14-vom_Erloeserkirchturm-2010-gje.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Jerusalem-Grabeskirche-14-vom_Erloeserkirchturm-2010-gje.jpg/330px-Jerusalem-Grabeskirche-14-vom_Erloeserkirchturm-2010-gje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Jerusalem-Grabeskirche-14-vom_Erloeserkirchturm-2010-gje.jpg/440px-Jerusalem-Grabeskirche-14-vom_Erloeserkirchturm-2010-gje.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jerusalem-Grabeskirche-14-vom_Erloeserkirchturm-2010-gje.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre" title="Church of the Holy Sepulchre">Church of the Holy Sepulchre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg/220px-Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg/330px-Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg/440px-Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kaaba_mirror_edit_jj.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">Kaaba</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Middle East lies at the juncture of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>. It is the birthplace and <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spiritual</a> center of religions such as <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manichaeism" title="Manichaeism">Manichaeism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yezidi" title="Yezidi">Yezidi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yarsan" title="Yarsan">Yarsan</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandeanism" title="Mandeanism">Mandeanism</a>, and in Iran, <a href="/wiki/Mithraism" title="Mithraism">Mithraism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manicheanism" title="Manicheanism">Manicheanism</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>. Throughout its history the Middle East has been a major center of world affairs; a strategically, economically, politically, culturally, and religiously sensitive area. The region is one of the regions where agriculture was independently discovered, and from the Middle East it was spread, during the Neolithic, to different regions of the world such as Europe, the Indus Valley and Eastern Africa.
</p><p>Prior to the formation of civilizations, advanced cultures formed all over the Middle East during the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a>. The search for agricultural lands by agriculturalists, and pastoral lands by herdsmen meant different migrations took place within the region and shaped its ethnic and demographic makeup.
</p><p>The Middle East is widely and most famously known as the <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">Cradle of civilization</a>. The world's earliest civilizations, <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">Akkad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">Babylonia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kish_civilization" title="Kish civilization">Kish</a> in the Levant, all originated in the Fertile Crescent and <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> Valley regions of the ancient Near East. These were followed by the <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurrians" title="Hurrians">Hurrian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urartian" title="Urartian">Urartian</a> civilisations of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">Asia Minor</a>; <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">Elam</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran" title="History of Iran">Persia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Median</a> civilizations in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, as well as the civilizations of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Levant" title="History of the Levant">Levant</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Ebla" title="Ebla">Ebla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mari,_Syria" title="Mari, Syria">Mari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tell_Brak" title="Tell Brak">Nagar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ugarit" title="Ugarit">Ugarit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramea" title="Aramea">Aramea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitanni" title="Mitanni">Mitanni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majan_(civilization)" title="Majan (civilization)">Magan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheba" title="Sheba">Sheba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iram_of_the_Pillars" title="Iram of the Pillars">Ubar</a>). The Near East was first largely unified under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo_Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo Assyrian Empire">Neo Assyrian Empire</a>, then the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> followed later by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_Empire" title="Macedonian Empire">Macedonian Empire</a> and after this to some degree by the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran" title="History of Iran">Iranian empires</a> (namely the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arsacid_Empire" title="Arsacid Empire">Parthian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" title="Sassanid Empire">Sassanid Empires</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>. The region served as the intellectual and economic center of the Roman Empire and played an exceptionally important role due to its periphery on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" title="Sassanid Empire">Sassanid Empire</a>. Thus, the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> stationed up to five or six of their legions in the region for the sole purpose of defending it from Sassanid and Bedouin raids and invasions.
</p><p>From the 4th century CE onwards, the Middle East became the center of the two main powers at the time, the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" title="Sassanid Empire">Sassanid Empire</a>. However, it would be the later <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Islamic Caliphates</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a> which began with the Islamic conquest of the region in the 7th century AD, that would first unify the entire Middle East as a distinct region and create the dominant <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arab</a> ethnic identity that largely (but not exclusively) persists today. The 4 caliphates that dominated the Middle East for more than 600 years were the <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun Caliphate</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umayyad_caliphate" title="Umayyad caliphate">Umayyad caliphate</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid_caliphate" title="Abbasid caliphate">Abbasid caliphate</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid_caliphate" title="Fatimid caliphate">Fatimid caliphate</a>. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a> would come to dominate the region, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(Antiquity)" title="Kingdom of Armenia (Antiquity)">Kingdom of Armenia</a> would incorporate parts of the region to their domain, the <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuks</a> would rule the region and spread Turko-Persian culture, and the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a> would found the <a href="/wiki/Crusader_states" title="Crusader states">Crusader states</a> that would stand for roughly two centuries. Josiah Russell estimates the population of what he calls "Islamic territory" as roughly 12.5 million in 1000 – <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> 8 million, <a href="/wiki/Syria_(region)" title="Syria (region)">Syria</a> 2 million, and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> 1.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussell1985298_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERussell1985298-38">[37]</a></sup>
From the 16th century onward, the Middle East came to be dominated, once again, by two main powers: the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid dynasty</a>.
</p><p>The modern Middle East began after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, when the Ottoman Empire, which was allied with the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>, was defeated by the British Empire and their allies and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partitioning_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Partitioning of the Ottoman Empire">partitioned</a> into a number of separate nations, initially under British and French Mandates. Other defining events in this transformation included the establishment of Israel in 1948 and the eventual departure of European powers, notably <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> by the end of the 1960s. They were supplanted in some part by the rising influence of the United States from the 1970s onwards.
</p><p>In the 20th century, the region's significant stocks of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> gave it new strategic and economic importance. Mass production of oil began around 1945, with Saudi Arabia, Iran, Kuwait, Iraq, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> having large quantities of oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Estimated <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves#Estimated_reserves_by_country" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a>, especially in Saudi Arabia and Iran, are some of the highest in the world, and the international oil cartel <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> is dominated by Middle Eastern countries.
</p><p>During the Cold War, the Middle East was a theater of ideological struggle between the two superpowers and their allies: <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the United States on one side, and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> on the other, as they competed to influence regional allies. Besides the political reasons there was also the "ideological conflict" between the two systems. Moreover, as <a href="/wiki/Louise_Fawcett" title="Louise Fawcett">Louise Fawcett</a> argues, among many important areas of contention, or perhaps more accurately of anxiety, were, first, the desires of the superpowers to gain strategic advantage in the region, second, the fact that the region contained some two-thirds of the world's oil reserves in a context where oil was becoming increasingly vital to the economy of the Western world [...]<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> Within this contextual framework, the United States sought to divert the Arab world from Soviet influence. Throughout the 20th and 21st centuries, the region has experienced both periods of relative peace and tolerance and periods of conflict particularly between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunnis</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shiite" title="Shiite">Shiites</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Middle_East" title="Demographics of the Middle East">Demographics of the Middle East</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_metropolitan_areas_of_the_Middle_East" title="Largest metropolitan areas of the Middle East">Largest metropolitan areas of the Middle East</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maunsell%27s_map,_Pre-World_War_I_British_Ethnographical_Map_of_eastern_Turkey_in_Asia,_Syria_and_western_Persia_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9183" data-file-width="10714" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Maunsell%27s_map%2C_Pre-World_War_I_British_Ethnographical_Map_of_eastern_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Syria_and_western_Persia_01.jpg/220px-Maunsell%27s_map%2C_Pre-World_War_I_British_Ethnographical_Map_of_eastern_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Syria_and_western_Persia_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Maunsell%27s_map%2C_Pre-World_War_I_British_Ethnographical_Map_of_eastern_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Syria_and_western_Persia_01.jpg/330px-Maunsell%27s_map%2C_Pre-World_War_I_British_Ethnographical_Map_of_eastern_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Syria_and_western_Persia_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Maunsell%27s_map%2C_Pre-World_War_I_British_Ethnographical_Map_of_eastern_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Syria_and_western_Persia_01.jpg/440px-Maunsell%27s_map%2C_Pre-World_War_I_British_Ethnographical_Map_of_eastern_Turkey_in_Asia%2C_Syria_and_western_Persia_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maunsell%27s_map,_Pre-World_War_I_British_Ethnographical_Map_of_eastern_Turkey_in_Asia,_Syria_and_western_Persia_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maunsell's map, a Pre-World War I British Ethnographical Map of the Middle East</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_the_Middle_East" title="Ethnic groups in the Middle East">Ethnic groups in the Middle East</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> constitute the largest ethnic group in the Middle East, followed by various <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranian peoples</a> and then by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkic_people" title="Turkic people">Turkic peoples</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azeris" title="Azeris">Azeris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Turkmen" title="Syrian Turkmen">Syrian Turkmen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmen" title="Iraqi Turkmen">Iraqi Turkmen</a>). Native ethnic groups of the region include, in addition to Arabs, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arameans_in_Syria" title="Arameans in Syria">Arameans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baloch_peoples" title="Baloch peoples">Baloch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copts" title="Copts">Copts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriots" title="Greek Cypriots">Greek Cypriots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lurs" title="Lurs">Lurs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandaeans" title="Mandaeans">Mandaeans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samaritans" title="Samaritans">Samaritans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shabak_people" title="Shabak people">Shabaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tat_people_(Iran)" title="Tat people (Iran)">Tats</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zazas" title="Zazas">Zazas</a>. European ethnic groups that form a diaspora in the region include <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Kabardians" title="Kabardians">Kabardians</a>), <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levantines_(Latin_Christians)" title="Levantines (Latin Christians)">Franco-Levantines</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levantines_(Latin_Christians)#Italian_Levantines" title="Levantines (Latin Christians)">Italo-Levantines</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens" title="Iraqi Turkmens">Iraqi Turkmens</a>. Among other migrant populations are <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="Filipinos in Saudi Arabia">Filipinos</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indians_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="Indians in Saudi Arabia">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesians_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="Indonesians in Saudi Arabia">Indonesians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistanis" title="Pakistanis">Pakistanis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pashtuns" title="Pashtuns">Pashtuns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Arab" title="Afro-Arab">Afro-Arabs</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span></h3>
<p>"Migration has always provided an important vent for labor market pressures in the Middle East. For the period between the 1970s and 1990s, the Arab states of the Persian Gulf in particular provided a rich source of employment for workers from Egypt, Yemen and the countries of the Levant, while Europe had attracted young workers from North African countries due both to proximity and the legacy of colonial ties between France and the majority of North African states."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hassan_and_Dyer_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hassan_and_Dyer-41">[40]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, there are 13 million first-generation migrants from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_nations" title="Arab nations">Arab nations</a> in the world, of which 5.8 reside in other Arab countries. Expatriates from Arab countries contribute to the circulation of financial and human capital in the region and thus significantly promote regional development. In 2009 Arab countries received a total of US$35.1 billion in <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittance</a> in-flows and remittances sent to <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> from other Arab countries are 40 to 190 per cent higher than trade revenues between these and other Arab countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">Somali Civil War</a> has greatly increased the size of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_diaspora" title="Somali diaspora">Somali diaspora</a>, as many of the best educated Somalis left for Middle Eastern countries as well as <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.
</p><p>Non-Arab Middle Eastern countries such as <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> are also subject to important migration dynamics.
</p><p>A fair proportion of those migrating from Arab nations are from ethnic and religious minorities facing racial and or religious persecution and are not necessarily ethnic Arabs, Iranians or Turks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Large numbers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" title="Kurdish people">Kurds</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_people" title="Jewish people">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_people" title="Greek people">Greeks</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_people" title="Armenian people">Armenians</a> as well as many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandean" title="Mandean">Mandeans</a> have left nations such as Iraq, Iran, Syria and Turkey for these reasons during the last century. In Iran, many religious minorities such as <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼís</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoroastrians" title="Zoroastrians">Zoroastrians</a> have left since the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Islamic Revolution of 1979</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Middle_East" title="Religion in the Middle East">Religion in the Middle East</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mosque.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Mosque.jpg/220px-Mosque.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Mosque.jpg/330px-Mosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Mosque.jpg/440px-Mosque.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mosque.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Islam is the largest religion in the Middle East. Here, Muslim men are <a href="/wiki/Prostration" title="Prostration">prostrating</a> during prayer in a mosque.</div></div></div>
<p>The Middle East is very diverse when it comes to <a href="/wiki/Major_religious_groups" title="Major religious groups">religions</a>, many of which originated there. <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the largest religion in the Middle East, but other faiths that originated there, such as <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> are also well represented. <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Middle_East" title="Christianity in the Middle East">Christian communities</a> have <a href="/wiki/Role_of_Christianity_in_civilization" title="Role of Christianity in civilization">played a vital role</a> in the Middle East,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> and they represent 40.5% of Lebanon, where the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Lebanon" title="President of Lebanon">Lebanese president</a>, half of the cabinet, and half of the parliament follow one of the various Lebanese Christian rites. There are also important minority religions like the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yarsanism" title="Yarsanism">Yarsanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">Yazidism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fuccaro_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fuccaro-47">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandaeism" title="Mandaeism">Mandaeism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shabak_people#Religious_beliefs" title="Shabak people">Shabakism</a>, and in ancient times the region was home to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Mesopotamian_religion" title="Ancient Mesopotamian religion">Mesopotamian religions</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Canaanite_religion" title="Ancient Canaanite religion">Canaanite religions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manichaeism" title="Manichaeism">Manichaeism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mithraic_mysteries" title="Mithraic mysteries">Mithraism</a> and various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monotheist" title="Monotheist">monotheist</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gnostic" title="Gnostic">gnostic</a> sects.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<p>The six top languages, in terms of numbers of speakers, are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_dialects" title="Arabic dialects">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_languages" title="Kurdish languages">Kurdish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew_languages" title="Hebrew languages">Hebrew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_Greek" title="Modern Greek">Greek</a>. Arabic and Hebrew represent the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Asiatic_languages" title="Afro-Asiatic languages">Afro-Asiatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">language family</a>. Persian, Kurdish and Greek belong to the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> language family. Turkish belongs to <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a> language family. About 20 minority languages are also spoken in the Middle East.
</p><p>Arabic, with all its dialects, is the most widely spoken language in the Middle East, with <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Literary Arabic</a> being official in all North African and in most West Asian countries. Arabic dialects are also spoken in some adjacent areas in neighbouring Middle Eastern non-Arab countries. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic branch</a> of the Afro-Asiatic languages. Several <a href="/wiki/Modern_South_Arabian_languages" title="Modern South Arabian languages">Modern South Arabian languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Mehri_language" title="Mehri language">Mehri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soqotri_language" title="Soqotri language">Soqotri</a> are also spoken Yemen and Oman. Another Semitic language such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramaic_language" title="Aramaic language">Aramaic</a> and its dialects are spoken mainly by <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandaeans" title="Mandaeans">Mandaeans</a>. There is also an <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Oasis Berber</a>-speaking community in Egypt where the language is also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siwa_language" title="Siwa language">Siwa</a>. It is a non-Semitic Afro-Asiatic language.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> is the second most spoken language. While it is primarily spoken in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and some border areas in neighbouring countries, the country is one of the region's largest and most populous. It belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Iranian_languages" title="Indo-Iranian languages">Indo-Iranian branch</a> of the family of <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a>. Other Western Iranic languages spoken in the region include <a href="/wiki/Achomi_language" title="Achomi language">Achomi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daylami_language" title="Daylami language">Daylami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_languages" title="Kurdish languages">Kurdish</a> dialects, <a href="/wiki/Semnani_language" title="Semnani language">Semmani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luri_language" title="Luri language">Lurish</a>, amongst many others.
</p><p>The third-most widely spoken language, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, is largely confined to Turkey, which is also one of the region's largest and most populous countries, but it is present in areas in neighboring countries. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic languages</a>, which have their origins in Central Asia. Another Turkic language, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>, is spoken by Azerbaijanis in Iran.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew_languages" title="Hebrew languages">Hebrew</a> is one of the two official languages of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, the other being Arabic. Hebrew is spoken and used by over 80% of Israel's population, the other 20% using Arabic.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Modern_Greek" title="Modern Greek">Greek</a> is one of the two official languages of <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, and the country's main language. Small communities of Greek speakers exist all around the Middle East; until the 20th century it was also widely spoken in Asia Minor (being the second most spoken language there, after Turkish) and Egypt. During the antiquity, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> for many areas of the western Middle East and until the Muslim expansion it was widely spoken there as well. Until the late 11th century, it was also the main spoken language in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">Asia Minor</a>; after that it was gradually replaced by the Turkish language as the Anatolian Turks expanded and the local Greeks were assimilated, especially in the interior.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1026" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg/170px-1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg/255px-1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg/340px-1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1911_Ottoman_Calendar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1911 Ottoman calendar shown in several different languages such as: Ottoman Turkish (in Arabic script), Greek, Armenian, Hebrew, Bulgarian, and French.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is one of the official languages of Akrotiri and Dhekelia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> It is also commonly taught and used as a second language, especially among the <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">middle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upper_class" title="Upper class">upper classes</a>, in countries such as <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan" title="Kurdistan">Kurdistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> It is also a main language in some Emirates of the United Arab Emirates. It is also spoken as native language by Jewish immigrants from Anglophone countries (UK, USA, Australia) in Israel and understood widely as second language there.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is taught and used in many government facilities and media in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, and is taught in some primary and secondary schools of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>. <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>, a Semitic language mainly spoken in Europe, is also used by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maltese_in_Egypt" title="Maltese in Egypt">Franco-Maltese diaspora</a> in Egypt. Also, due to widespread immigration of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Jews" title="French Jews">French Jews</a> to <a href="/wiki/French_Jews_in_Israel" title="French Jews in Israel">Israel</a>, it is the native language of approximately 200,000 Jews of Israel.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a> speakers are also to be found in the region. <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a> is spoken by the Georgian diaspora. 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> is spoken by a large portion of the Israeli population, because of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aliyah_from_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States_in_the_1990s" title="Aliyah from the Commonwealth of Independent States in the 1990s">emigration in the late 1990s</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDowty200495_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDowty200495-53">[52]</a></sup> Russian today is a popular unofficial language in use in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>; news, radio and sign boards can be found in Russian around the country after Hebrew and Arabic. <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Caucasian_languages" title="Northwest Caucasian languages">Circassian</a> is also spoken by the diaspora in the region and by almost all Circassians in Israel who speak Hebrew and English as well. 
</p><p>The largest <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>-speaking community in the Middle East is found in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, where as of 1995<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Middle_East&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Romanian is spoken by 5% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[note 2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> are widely spoken by migrant communities in many Middle Eastern countries, such as Saudi Arabia (where 20–25% of the population is South Asian), the United Arab Emirates (where 50–55% of the population is South Asian), and Qatar, which have large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladeshi</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> immigrants.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Middle_East" title="Economy of the Middle East">Economy of the Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_economic_integration" title="Middle East economic integration">Middle East economic integration</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Ambox current red Americas.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 1.5x,
