class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2016</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oil_and_Gas_Infrastructure_Persian_Gulf_(large).gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="844" data-file-width="959" decoding="async" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Oil_and_Gas_Infrastructure_Persian_Gulf_%28large%29.gif/300px-Oil_and_Gas_Infrastructure_Persian_Gulf_%28large%29.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Oil_and_Gas_Infrastructure_Persian_Gulf_%28large%29.gif/450px-Oil_and_Gas_Infrastructure_Persian_Gulf_%28large%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Oil_and_Gas_Infrastructure_Persian_Gulf_%28large%29.gif/600px-Oil_and_Gas_Infrastructure_Persian_Gulf_%28large%29.gif 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oil_and_Gas_Infrastructure_Persian_Gulf_(large).gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a> pipelines in the Middle-East</div></div></div>
<p>Middle Eastern economies range from being very poor (such as Gaza and Yemen) to extremely wealthy nations (such as Qatar and UAE). Overall, as of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Middle_East&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, according to the CIA World Factbook, all nations in the Middle East are maintaining a positive rate of growth.
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>'s <i>World Development Indicators</i> database published on July 1, 2009, the three largest Middle Eastern economies in 2008 were Turkey ($794,228), Saudi Arabia ($467,601) and Iran ($385,143) in terms of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">Nominal GDP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WB-GDP-Nominal_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-WB-GDP-Nominal-57">[55]</a></sup> Regarding nominal GDP per capita, the highest ranking countries are Qatar ($93,204), the UAE ($55,028), Kuwait ($45,920) and Cyprus ($32,745).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> Turkey ($1,028,897), Iran ($839,438) and Saudi Arabia ($589,531) had the largest economies in terms of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">GDP-PPP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WB-GDP-PPP_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-WB-GDP-PPP-59">[57]</a></sup> When it comes to per capita (PPP)-based income, the highest-ranking countries are Qatar ($86,008), Kuwait ($39,915), the UAE ($38,894), Bahrain ($34,662) and Cyprus ($29,853). The lowest-ranking country in the Middle East, in terms of per capita income (PPP), is the autonomous Palestinian Authority of Gaza and the West Bank ($1,100).
</p><p>The economic structure of Middle Eastern nations are different in the sense that while some nations are heavily dependent on export of only oil and oil-related products (such as Saudi Arabia, the UAE and Kuwait), others have a highly diverse economic base (such as Cyprus, Israel, Turkey and Egypt). Industries of the Middle Eastern region include oil and oil-related products, agriculture, cotton, cattle, dairy, textiles, leather products, surgical instruments, defence equipment (guns, ammunition, tanks, submarines, fighter jets, UAVs, and missiles). Banking is also an important sector of the economies, especially in the case of UAE and Bahrain.
</p><p>With the exception of Cyprus, Turkey, Egypt, Lebanon and Israel, tourism has been a relatively undeveloped area of the economy, in part because of the socially conservative nature of the region as well as political turmoil in certain regions of the Middle East. In recent years, however, countries such as the UAE, Bahrain, and Jordan have begun attracting greater numbers of tourists because of improving tourist facilities and the relaxing of tourism-related restrictive policies.
</p><p>Unemployment is notably high in the Middle East and North Africa region, particularly among young people aged 15–29, a demographic representing 30% of the region's total population. The total regional unemployment rate in 2005, according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a>, was 13.2%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> and among youth is as high as 25%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> up to 37% in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and 73% in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span></h2>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa" title="Climate change in the Middle East and North Africa">Climate change in the Middle East and North Africa</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Middle_East_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Middle East map of Köppen climate classification</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Northern_Africa_future.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1691" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Northern_Africa_future.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Northern_Africa_future.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Northern_Africa_future.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Northern_Africa_future.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Northern_Africa_future.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Northern_Africa_future.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Northern_Africa_future.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Predicted <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> map for North Africa for 2071–2100</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa" title="Climate change in the Middle East and North Africa">Climate change in the Middle East and North Africa</a> (MENA) refers to changes in the <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> of the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">MENA region</a> and the subsequent response, adaption and mitigation strategies of countries in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> In 2018, the MENA region emitted 3.2 billion tonnes of carbon dioxide and produced 8.7% of global <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> (GHG)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:022_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:022-64">[62]</a></sup> despite making up only 6% of the global population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> These emissions are mostly from the <a href="/wiki/Energy_industry" title="Energy industry">energy sector</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> an integral component of many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern" title="Middle Eastern">Middle Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North African</a> economies due to the extensive <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> reserves that are found within the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> The region of Middle East is one of the most <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_vulnerability" title="Climate change vulnerability">vulnerable to climate change</a>. The impacts include increase in <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">drought</a> conditions, aridity, <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heatwaves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a>.
</p><p>Sharp global temperature and sea level changes, shifting precipitation patterns and increased frequency of <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events are some of the main impacts of climate change as identified by the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> (IPCC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:143_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:143-69">[67]</a></sup> The MENA region is especially vulnerable to such impacts due to its arid and semi-arid environment, facing climatic challenges such as low rainfall, high temperatures and dry soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:143_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:143-69">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:62_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:62-70">[68]</a></sup> The climatic conditions that foster such challenges for MENA are projected by the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">IPCC</a> to worsen throughout the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:143_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:143-69">[67]</a></sup> If <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> are not significantly reduced, part of the MENA region risks becoming uninhabitable before the year 2100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_Weforum2_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_Weforum2-71">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_Euroactive2_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_Euroactive2-72">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate change</a> is expected to put significant strain on already <a href="/wiki/Water_conflict_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa" title="Water conflict in the Middle East and North Africa">scarce water</a> and agricultural resources within the MENA region, threatening the national security and political stability of all included countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:324_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_:324-74">[72]</a></sup> This has prompted some MENA countries to engage with the issue of climate change on an international level through environmental accords such as the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a>. Law and policy are also being established on a national level amongst MENA countries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_Routledge_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa_Routledge-75">[73]</a></sup> with a focus on the development of renewable energies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup></div></div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In Italian, the expression "Vicino Oriente" (Near East) was also widely used to refer to Turkey, and <i>Estremo Oriente</i> (Far East or Extreme East) to refer to all of Asia east of Middle East</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the 1993 <i>Statistical Abstract of Israel</i> there were 250,000 Romanian speakers in Israel, at a population of 5,548,523 (census 1995).</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
